<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41705648-69cf-43e3-8e5a-adcd06cad154'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer7399009714703777740"><i>In a manor by the sea, twelve sisters are cursed.</i><br/><br/>Annaleigh lives a sheltered life at Highmoor, a manor by the sea, with her sisters, their father, and stepmother. Once they were twelve, but loneliness fills the grand halls now that four of the girls' lives have been cut short. Each death was more tragic than the last—the plague, a plummeting fall, a drowning, a slippery pl</span>
  <span id="freeText7399009714703777740" style="display:none"><i>In a manor by the sea, twelve sisters are cursed.</i><br /><br />Annaleigh lives a sheltered life at Highmoor, a manor by the sea, with her sisters, their father, and stepmother. Once they were twelve, but loneliness fills the grand halls now that four of the girls' lives have been cut short. Each death was more tragic than the last—the plague, a plummeting fall, a drowning, a slippery plunge—and there are whispers throughout the surrounding villages that the family is cursed by the gods.<br /><br />Disturbed by a series of ghostly visions, Annaleigh becomes increasingly suspicious that the deaths were no accidents. Her sisters have been sneaking out every night to attend glittering balls, dancing until dawn in silk gowns and shimmering slippers, and Annaleigh isn't sure whether to try to stop them or to join their forbidden trysts. Because who—or what—are they really dancing with?<br /><br />When Annaleigh's involvement with a mysterious stranger who has secrets of his own intensifies, it's a race to unravel the darkness that has fallen over her family—before it claims her next.</span>

<div id="review_2945513843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2945513843" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2945513843?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2945513843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12558160590563126444">5 SPOOKY, TERRIFYING, OH MY GOD MY HANDS STILL TREMBLING , CONTAINING GOTHIC ELEMENTS, GHOSTS AND CURSES KINDA STORY, PLEASE LEAVE YOUR LIGHTS ON BEFORE GO TO SLEEP AFTER THIS BOOK AND DON’T BE AFRAID OF CREAKING SOUNDS, THEY MIGHT BE ONLY RATS DANCING ON YOUR FLOORS STARS!<br/><br/>You know Brother Grimm’s fairy-tale named “Twelve Dancing Princesses”: Those girls each more beautiful than the last, sleep in twelve beds in the same room. Every night their doors securely locked by their father. But in the m</span>
  <span id="freeText12558160590563126444" style="display:none">5 SPOOKY, TERRIFYING, OH MY GOD MY HANDS STILL TREMBLING , CONTAINING GOTHIC ELEMENTS, GHOSTS AND CURSES KINDA STORY, PLEASE LEAVE YOUR LIGHTS ON BEFORE GO TO SLEEP AFTER THIS BOOK AND DON’T BE AFRAID OF CREAKING SOUNDS, THEY MIGHT BE ONLY RATS DANCING ON YOUR FLOORS STARS!<br /><br />You know Brother Grimm’s fairy-tale named “Twelve Dancing Princesses”: Those girls each more beautiful than the last, sleep in twelve beds in the same room. Every night their doors securely locked by their father. But in the morning THEIR DANCE SHOES are found to be WORN THROUGH as they had been DANCING ALL NIGHT! So this book’s quite great, horrific, roller coaster riding version of retelling. <br /><br /> As you consider how Grimm Brothers’ vulgar, harsh tones and merciless writing on those books and depressing, grimacing things happened to their characters, you may understand how this book could give you creeps, stomach churning, eerie sensation. THIS IS REALLY SCARY AND MIND BENDING BOOK! If you’re not ready to read something spooky, twisty, surprising, giving you nightmares, please put the book down and choose something lighter like your chic-lits or summer reading you could grab to read at the seaside while you’re sipping your cool drink and totally forget about this dark story forever!<br /><br />This book might be 12 Dances Princesses’ retelling, a different approach, newer version but it also reminded me the “Inception” with its mind confusing, head hurting, dream into-dream into- dream sequences. You’re really getting lost what’s real or what’s a nightmare. There are some parts of “7 Ravens” which is originally about 7 brothers but we had our heroine Annaleigh ( which is so amazingly melodic and capturing name, if I ever have a child, I named after her without thinking a second) and her 7 sisters! And also we had some glimpses of Little Women in this book as we read the sister’s stories and character analysis. Rosalie reminded me Amy and Verity had a little Beth, a little Amy inside. And Camille, know-it all, pretentious elder sister reminded me a little Meg, at least Annaleigh and her struggles had great resemblances with Meg and Joe’s fighting about their differences.<br /><br /> WHAT I REALLY REALLY REALLY LIKE ABOUT THIS BOOK:<br /><br />BIG FAN OF RETELLINGS AND THIS GREAT DEBUT :<br />It’s real defying and challenging thing to write again with brand new, fresh, crystal clear, visionary perspective and create a new story based on Brother Grimms’ works. The author chose not one of the famous works of him and she definitely achieved dexterous, adroit, refined job by adding horrific, gothic, mysterious elements and a poignant, lyrical romantic story.<br /><br /> <br />FAST PACING TEMPO, HEART-THROBBING TERRIFYING SCENES:<br /><br />Verity acts like Sixth Sense’s Haley Joel Osment and claims she’s talking with the ghosts of her dead sisters and draws so many scary paintings which contain too many gory and harmful details about the way how her sisters have died. There is no way she can know these facts without being crime scenes (which of course she hasn’t!)<br />I really jump out of my seat, throw the book away as if my hands were burned, screamed non-stop when I caught a monster looking back at the me(then I realized that’s my morning self in the mirror before I had my morning coffee so I shut my mouth!)<br /><br />AMAZING LOVE STORY:<br />We need romance after jumping out of our seats and taking few breathes to ease our heavy heart rates! So this love story was a medicine for the pain this book gave me. I love Annaleigh and Cassius’ slow-burn, passionate, tender, devoted, growing love story. <br /><br />ENDING:<br />The part about the villain’s identity was foreseeable but last twists about delusions were clearly mind-bending, brain cell burning, head thudding kind of experiences they had to endure for finishing this book. I enjoyed those twists, mind games that the author professionally played with us. She was my great winner.<br /><br />SUMMARY:<br />I want to read more retellings and surprising stories if Erin A. Craig intends to write. This year, I discovered too many new writers and I enjoyed their works so much which gave me hope, we’ll have more amazing literary works in near future. I LOVE THIS BOOK TOO MUCH. If you’re big fans mysterious, horrifying, Grimm Brothers style fairy-tales, that’s definitely a “Yes, this book is truly for you!”<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12558160590563126444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2679060266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2679060266" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2679060266?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2679060266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2242217696936706256"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603726934ra/30291570.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>...and the award for <b>Exceptional New Voice in YA Horror</b> goes to...<br/><br/><b>ERIN A. CRAIG</b>!!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566768176ra/28050473.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>((the crowd goes wild))</i><br/><br/>I loved this book <u>so, so much</u>. It was not at all what I expected, but I am so damned pleased with what it turned out to be.<br/><br/>In one word, <b>EVERYTHING</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566768176ra/28050472.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Annaleigh lives at <i>Highmoor</i>, a remote manor on the sea with her father, stepmother and sisters. Where once there were twelve sisters, at the start of our story, only nine remain. <br/><br/>The most recent to die, Eulalie, plunged to her death from a high cli</span>
  <span id="freeText2242217696936706256" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603726934ra/30291570.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...and the award for <b>Exceptional New Voice in YA Horror</b> goes to...<br><br><b>ERIN A. CRAIG</b>!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566768176ra/28050473.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>((the crowd goes wild))</i><br><br>I loved this book <u>so, so much</u>. It was not at all what I expected, but I am so damned pleased with what it turned out to be.<br><br>In one word, <b>EVERYTHING</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566768176ra/28050472.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Annaleigh lives at <i>Highmoor</i>, a remote manor on the sea with her father, stepmother and sisters. Where once there were twelve sisters, at the start of our story, only nine remain. <br><br>The most recent to die, Eulalie, plunged to her death from a high cliff to the sea. It is rumored she was out to meet a lover with whom she was planning to run away.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566918835ra/28059164.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tragedy has struck the family so many times, the villagers whisper they are cursed. <br><br>While some of her sisters believe in the validity of a family curse, Annaleigh doesn't. She also doesn't believe that Eulalie's death was an accident. <br><br>Perhaps her other sister's deaths weren't accidental either?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566141421ra/28011175.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Teaming up with a handsome and mysterious stranger, Annaleigh begins to investigate what is truly happening at <i>Highmoor</i>.<br><br>As many of you may know, <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> is a retelling of a classic fairy tale known as <i>The Shoes That Were Danced To Pieces</i>, or <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501786471ra/23499018.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Going into this, I expected a typical YA fairy tale retelling. Fortunately, there was nothing typical about this book.<br><br>Truth be told, a lot of this story creeped me the heck out.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565004886ra/27941834.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was one night, I was up late, reading this on my kindle with all the lights turned off, I got to a section where there is a particularly lucid scene involving one of Annaleigh's dead sisters and I legit almost put that bitch in the freezer! <br><br>I had to switch to something light and fluffy just to be able to go to sleep that night.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547915085ra/26942355.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As someone who is a great fan of the dark and macabre, I must say, I was beyond impressed with Craig's writing. <br><br>Her ability to conjure truly terrifying moments and atmosphere is absolutely fantastic.<br><br>I am calling this a YA Horror, because even though the story isn't exactly a Horror story, I am calling out Erin A. Craig as a Horror writer! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590942301ra/29572578.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really hope she continues more in that vein with her future stories. <br><br>There was an ominous feeling surrounding this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The fae-like feeling of the portal door bringing the sisters to the balls <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, it was all incredibly visceral.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566918835ra/28059163.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have never read the original source material, so I cannot weigh in on the merits of this as a retelling but I imagine, most folks who have read the original will be impressed. <br><br>In my opinion, this book has it all and if you are a fan of gothic-feeling stories, you CANNOT miss this one. Pick it up, you won't regret it!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553036360ra/27233877.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you so much to the publisher, Delacorte Press, for providing me with a copy to read and review. <br><br>I cannot wait to see what Craig comes up with next. You better believe I will be buying it!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2937962774" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2937962774" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2937962774?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2937962774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6593549093713171637"><b>
  <i>‘show me debauched nightmares or sunniest daydreams. come not as you are but as you wish to be seen.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>uhhh… theres definitely gonna be nightmares. how come no one told me this would be so creepy?!? wow. im such a wimp. lol.<br/><br/>also, early side note. i had no idea this was a retelling before i picked it up. ive never even heard of <i>‘the twelve dancing princesses,’</i> so im coming at this review with the perspective that this story is wildly original and one of a kind, because i have no idea which aspe</span>
  <span id="freeText6593549093713171637" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘show me debauched nightmares or sunniest daydreams. come not as you are but as you wish to be seen.’</i>
</b><br /><br />uhhh… theres definitely gonna be nightmares. how come no one told me this would be so creepy?!? wow. im such a wimp. lol.<br /><br />also, early side note. i had no idea this was a retelling before i picked it up. ive never even heard of <i>‘the twelve dancing princesses,’</i> so im coming at this review with the perspective that this story is wildly original and one of a kind, because i have no idea which aspects are part of the retelling and which are craigs own invention. <br /><br />that being said, if <i>‘to kill a kingdom’</i> and <i>‘the wicked deep’</i> created a hybrid world, it would be the atmosphere and setting of <i>‘house of salt and sorrows.’</i> its not exactly enchanting, because the story is actually quite dark. but there is something so captivating about a mysterious island kingdom, a family curse, and unreliable events. the writing easily transports the reader into this world, filled with ghosts and secrets, and that alone made this story worth it to me. <br /><br />however, i am a little disappointed with the ending. there are a couple of things that relate to their religion/gods that come into play and it had me very confused. im not sure if i missed their introduction earlier on in the novel, but i felt like that key component was quite rushed. could just be an oversight on my part, though. <br /><br />regardless, this is a hauntingly impressive debut!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6593549093713171637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2677698187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677698187" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677698187?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42766858-house-of-salt-and-sorrows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=book-subscriptions">book-subscriptions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677698187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1104105842928175960"><b>BOTM YA selection August 2019!</b><br/><br/><b>3.5 STARS</b><br/><br/><i>"As they whispered their strained condolences, I noticed the guests were careful to not get too close. Was it in deference to our station, or were they worried something might rub off? I wanted to chalk it up to the lowbrow superstition, but as a distant aunt approached me, a thin smile on her thin lips, the same question lingered in her eyes, just below the surface, impossible to miss: Which one of us would be next?"</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1562848977ra/27810294.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh yes, I love a good book that is unafr</span>
  <span id="freeText1104105842928175960" style="display:none"><b>BOTM YA selection August 2019!</b><br><br><b>3.5 STARS</b><br><br><i>"As they whispered their strained condolences, I noticed the guests were careful to not get too close. Was it in deference to our station, or were they worried something might rub off? I wanted to chalk it up to the lowbrow superstition, but as a distant aunt approached me, a thin smile on her thin lips, the same question lingered in her eyes, just below the surface, impossible to miss: Which one of us would be next?"</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1562848977ra/27810294.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh yes, I love a good book that is unafraid to pull a few punches. Here's the thing; initially, I was drawn to this book for three reasons: it's a fairytale retelling, it has a gorgeous cover, and it's got the whole romantic horror aspect down pat. <i>Is this a sub-genre? YA romance horror? If not, it certainly should be.</i> Overall, this one delivered, and I'm intrigued to see more from Erin A. Craig in the future. <br><br>Like I stated above, this is a YA retelling of a somewhat obscure fairytale by the Brother's Grimm called <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>. In the original version, things are much more tame and boring, so naturally I prefer the author's reimagined tale to the original. Instead of princesses being caught sneaking out and then given in marriage to the man who was able to solve the mystery of the worn out shoes, we have sisters who are dying in disturbing, and somewhat unbelievable ways, which explains why our protagonist is so determined to figure out just what in the beard of Moses is going on. Part fantasy, part murder mystery, this is an ambitious book, especially for a debut author, and I think she pulled the entire thing off rather well. <br><br>The most controversial topic surrounding this book, at least that I've seen, is the amount of disturbing content included in this novel, so let's start there. Personally, I loved it, but if you are sensitive to disturbing violence, gore, blood, and discussions of suicide, this may not be the book for you. Many scenes are quite descriptive, and there are tons of difficult, yet necessary themes discussed here that may be more appropriate for the upper end of the YA spectrum. There is a definite gothic fantasy feel to the story, which gives it an appropriate darkness, but this is contrasted with an equal dose of romance-complete with a HEA!<br><br>I think my main concern is that this is the slowest of slow burns until about 2/3 through the novel. I appreciated all of the atmospheric setup, but it also felt as if there wasn't a bit of action until the explosion of a climax. However, the twist was excellent, and the entire reimagining was creative and unique, which makes me glad I spent the time plowing through the slower moments. A solid, beautifully written debut, and I hope to see more from the author in the near future. Also? I hope we get more retellings from Craig, because she clearly has a knack for dark fantasy. <br><br><i>*I received a review copy from the publisher via NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1104105842928175960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2704296243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2704296243" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2704296243?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2704296243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7808012069317372352"><i>In a manor by the sea, twelve sisters are cursed..</i><br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>Annaleigh, (who BTW, doesn't love this name?) lives at Highmoor, a Manor by the sea with her father, his new wife and her eleven sisters. Tragedy seems to be hitting this family hard, perhaps it is cursed? The villagers think so. This used to be a big happy family. But after their Mother died, the family went into mourning, then four of her sisters died one by one. Annaleigh begins to believe that her sister's deaths are not accidents. <br/><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText7808012069317372352" style="display:none"><i>In a manor by the sea, twelve sisters are cursed..</i><br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br />Annaleigh, (who BTW, doesn't love this name?) lives at Highmoor, a Manor by the sea with her father, his new wife and her eleven sisters. Tragedy seems to be hitting this family hard, perhaps it is cursed? The villagers think so. This used to be a big happy family. But after their Mother died, the family went into mourning, then four of her sisters died one by one. Annaleigh begins to believe that her sister's deaths are not accidents. <br /><br />After the latest death, her Stepmother convinces her father that they should stop mourning and dress in beautiful clothing again, have balls and embrace life. Everyone but Annaleigh is on board, but she finally agrees to make her father happy. The new clothing and fairy shoes are not the only new things...the girls also become aware of a secret passage. A passage, or crevice if you will, that will take them to another place, a place of balls and dances, new encounters and new adventures. <br /><br />But tragedy strikes again when another sister goes missing....<br /><br />Put me in the camp of enjoying re-telling of fairy tales. In this case, this book is an atmospheric retelling of the Brother Grimm's "The Twelves Dancing Princesses" also known as "The Worn-out Dancing shoes and "The Shoes that were danced to Pieces." Sometimes re-telling’s can be campy but this one was not. I loved the atmosphere. The Manor overlooking the sea, the water, the sea creatures, the sisters, the balls, etc. This one felt atmospheric, Gothic and enchanting all at the same time. Is the family cursed? Why are the women of this family dying? <br /><br />The book does get darker at the end, but I enjoyed how the book built up to the ending. This book also had me questioning what was real and what wasn't as Annaleigh begins to question what is happening to her family. This is a great rainy day/escape book. It's full of atmosphere, magic, a little romance, mystery, and ghosts. Parts felt a little predictable, i.e. the love triangle, but this is YA so that often goes with the genre. I found this to be a very visual book as in, I could easily visualize what was happening as the Author did a great job with her descriptions.<br /><br />The Author is off to a very solid start with this debut novel. <br /><br />I received a copy of this book from Random House Children's and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. The thoughts and opinions expressed in this review are my own.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2763964252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2763964252" />
    <a title="MischaS_" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12772859-mischas"><img alt="MischaS_" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585808485p2/12772859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2763964252?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MischaS_" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MischaS_" href="/user/show/12772859-mischas">MischaS_</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=amazing-cover">amazing-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=english">english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=scary">scary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=blew-my-mind">blew-my-mind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2763964252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13277806073768926581">So, when I went to sleep last night (more like this night since it was after midnight), I kept thinking about what I'm going to say about this book. <br/>And I was drawing a blank. But let me just tell you, fantastic debut! This author is definitely staying on my radar. Plus massive praise for a stand-alone. <br/><br/>So, let's start at the beginning; my interest in this book started when I saw the gorgeous cover! It's just so pretty. Then I knew there were twelve sisters and a curse. And that's it, I know, I </span>
  <span id="freeText13277806073768926581" style="display:none">So, when I went to sleep last night (more like this night since it was after midnight), I kept thinking about what I'm going to say about this book. <br />And I was drawing a blank. But let me just tell you, fantastic debut! This author is definitely staying on my radar. Plus massive praise for a stand-alone. <br /><br />So, let's start at the beginning; my interest in this book started when I saw the gorgeous cover! It's just so pretty. Then I knew there were twelve sisters and a curse. And that's it, I know, I know, I pretty bad at knowing what's the book about before reading it. That's just the story of my life. <br />It was actually pretty surprising for me when at around the 34 % mark, I realised that this book was actually a retelling. And of one of my childhood favourite fairytale. The 12 dancing princesses, I adored that fairytale so much, if only because we had an illustrated book of the Grimm's fairytales and I loved just to look at all the pretty dresses the princesses had. <br />Of course, this book is getting extra points for being a retelling of this fairytale, plus some extra points because I never saw a retelling of this fairytale, you see all the cinderellas, beauties and beasts but this was rather original as far as retellings go.<br /><br />We start right in the action... okay, I know it's pretty bold of me calling a funeral action, but it does throw you into the story right away. It gives a space for the main character to reflect on all the dead sisters and on those of them who as still alive. I have to say that I found it easier to distinguish the dead ones than the living one. <br />Ava, Octavia, Elizabeth, Eulalie all died in more or less suspicious ways. And now Camille is the oldest one, the heir to their father's estate. Annaleigh is our main character and has the worst timing ever! She asked her father to talk about something always in the worst moments possible. But then the issues start. You have Lenore, Rosalie and Ligeia who are triplets. And the rest were Honor, Mercy and Verity collectively called the Graces. I have to say that I had a problem to remember all of these characters and especially to distinguish between them. <br /><br />The girls live with their father, who recently married a very young girl named Morella, she is not from the island, and she does not know their culture and customs. Generally, Morella was just so clueless that I had a very hard time deciding if she's truly that "stupid" or if she's secretly an evil step-mother. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She went on to announce that she was pregnant with a boy at the wake after Eulalie's funeral! Plus she had a very rude awakening when she found out that no matter how many sons she had, they would go to the back of the line when it came to the inheritance.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I was also unsure when it came to daddy-dearest. Annaleigh said that her father was nice and never violent right at the beginning of the story. However, his behaviour was anything but nice. <br /><br />Then we got Fisher who I disliked. He seemed like the friend who did not care about the girl until there was another guy interested. I feared a bit that it would end in a love-triangle, but thankfully it did not. And as for Cassius, he was a cutie, but I wish he had a bigger role in the story. Or maybe not. Because this way, the romance did not become the most important part of the story, rather the sprinkle on top. <br /><br />And now to the important part. I loved this story so much! It was sometimes so scary (especially when I wanted to read the last chapter before going to bed) that I even had to look under my bed. It left me speechless, worried to take a breath and wanting to get more. And then the rhythm would shift to a soothing one. And then a shock once again!<br />And then the last 25 % got so scary and crazy that it's a true retelling in a Grimm fashion! The end of the story is just the best; it got so mysterious and really creepy. Yeah, here I wish this mysterious aspect was introduced much earlier in the story. You could see little bits dropped here and there, but I never grasped the whole thing.<br />Because I did not see the ending coming at all, I was pretty much freaking out and thinking "What's even going on?!" And then the whole story flipped and all I knew or thought I knew crumbled under my eyes. <br />I'm not even going to say what the huge plot twist was, not even under the spoiler tag, it was just that crazy, but I may say that it reminded me a bit of the Mara Dyer series in the sense that nothing could have been trusted. <br /><br />But you know me, I have to have little grievances with the story, and this time it's that I could actually do without the epilogue. If I'm going to re-read this book, I'll skip the epilogue. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13277806073768926581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9552315457067509565">This started out pretty good but went downhill towards the end in my opinion. <br/><br/>First of all, I really enjoyed the atmosphere the author created here. It was perfect for a cold, stormy October night. I also liked the way how stuff (especially clothing) was described, it was easy to imagine how things looked like. <br/><br/>The characters themselves were okay overall, nothing special but not terrible either (gotta say though, I never quite remembered who was who so that's kinda bad).   <span id="freeText9552315457067509565" style="display:none">This started out pretty good but went downhill towards the end in my opinion. <br /><br />First of all, I really enjoyed the atmosphere the author created here. It was perfect for a cold, stormy October night. I also liked the way how stuff (especially clothing) was described, it was easy to imagine how things looked like. <br /><br />The characters themselves were okay overall, nothing special but not terrible either (gotta say though, I never quite remembered who was who so that's kinda bad). And sadly the love story was completely unnecessary and underdeveloped. <br /><br />Especially the mystery is where it went wrong for me. <br />I was intrigued in the beginning, came up with a few theories myself. But unfortunately the way it was resolved was just weirdly boring and over the top at the same time. I don't want to say "I could've done it better" because I definitely couldn't have regarding writing and stuff but I did prefer one of my theories over what actually happened. <br /><br />So, overall a mediocre read for me.</span>

<div id="review_2630120816" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2630120816" />
    <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance"><img alt="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600345081p2/53419883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2630120816?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2630120816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7662304788078369327">I am <br/>• spooked, <br/>• in love, <br/>• and broken.<br/><br/>The House of Salt and Sorrows is an enchanting and haunting retelling of the Brother Grimm’s fairy tale <b>
  <i>“Die Zwölf Tanzenden Prinzessinnen“</i>
</b>,“ The Twelve Dancing Princesses" (or sometimes referred to as "The Worn-Out Dancing Shoes" or "The Shoes that were Danced to Pieces"). Erin A. Craig’s spin on the tale delivers a magically engrossing tale including gods, a suspicious stepmother, magic doorways, haunting visions, terrifying suspense, and sweet roman</span>
  <span id="freeText7662304788078369327" style="display:none">I am <br />• spooked, <br />• in love, <br />• and broken.<br /><br />The House of Salt and Sorrows is an enchanting and haunting retelling of the Brother Grimm’s fairy tale <b>
  <i>“Die Zwölf Tanzenden Prinzessinnen“</i>
</b>,“ The Twelve Dancing Princesses" (or sometimes referred to as "The Worn-Out Dancing Shoes" or "The Shoes that were Danced to Pieces"). Erin A. Craig’s spin on the tale delivers a magically engrossing tale including gods, a suspicious stepmother, magic doorways, haunting visions, terrifying suspense, and sweet romance. A pot of gold for lovers of YA books and fairy tale retellings. <br /><br /><b>THIS MADE MY ‘BEST OF 2019’ BOOKLIST</b> in the YA genre!<br /><br /><b>“I dwelt alone, in a world of moan, and my soul was a stagnant tide <br /> Till the fair and gentle Eulalie became my blushing bride”</b><br /><br /><br />Highmore is the manor perched high above the sea on an island that houses a duke and his 12 daughters. The place has seen its share of grief in the last months as mysterious deaths are taking one daughter after another. A forsaken, haunted place is what the people on the mainland call the island, and a dark and hopeless mood has spread among the family. <br /><br />After another funeral underway, Annaleigh and her sisters protest the short mourning period their new stepmother imposes. After only a day, she has invited a dress- and shoemaker to cheer the girls up. Amazed and happy, the girls are having a wonderful time getting spoiled, but Annaleigh stays suspicious. She is haunted by the unexplained deaths of her sisters and shocked at the awful graphic drawings of death one of her little sisters makes.<br /><br />The girls are full of cheer and via a secret crevice near the burial chamber down by the sea they slip through and start attending the most spectacular dance balls they have ever imagined. Reluctantly, Annaleigh lets her guard down and finds herself whisked away dancing the nights away. <br />When an old friend and a new love interest are invited to the manor, Annaleigh’s haunted dreams become darker and stronger. And then, another sister goes missing!<br /><br />As the duke is wondering how his daughters keep going through their new shoes over and over, Annaleigh finds herself in a mystery she has to solve but does not know whom to trust. All the right people are at the wrong place at the wrong time and evil slowly spreads the halls of the manor. <br />Will Annaleigh solve the murders before the visions of her own death become true? <br />A sweet dark tale, not to be missed!<br /><br />***<br /><br />This novel had me by the neck! Not the first 1/3 of the book, but all after. This is Erin A. Craigs debut novel, and I am at awe at her ability to create stunningly haunting scenes. I actually went back and reread many of them, because I was thinking, ‘how did she do that’? Without fanfare, Annaleigh’s haunted moments were chilling and full of suspense. <b>Un-put-down-able!</b><br /><br />As for the first part of the novel, the dress-up, and the balls, they were glamorous, sparkly and enchanting – fairytale like. A sweet combo in a YA book, for the young at heart. That part didn’t grab me like the rest of the novel, but I am not the age of the intended audience.<br /> <br />I really enjoyed the entire premise and fairy tale retellings are a thing. Complete with a stepmother, a mystery and some romance, a perfect book to escape in. It’s been a very long time since I have heard the Grimm’s tale of <i>“Die Zwölf Tanzenden Prinzessinnen“</i>, but I definitely want to reread and compare. Check out a short synopsis of the original on my blog. <br /><br />If you like retellings, this is a must and I hope you will love it as I did. <br /><br />I received a digital copy of this novel from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. All opinions are my own. Thank you. <br /><br />My blog and more reviews:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/blog/2019/3/28/house-of-salt-and-sorrows">https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/blog...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7662304788078369327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2742709339015582755">TW: all your typical horror stuff - death, gore, ghosts, etc <br/><br/>This was a WILD ride. I don’t remember the last time I binge read a book so fast. I very rarely read anything close to horror (and this is as close as I get!) but this maintained a sense of eerie foreboding, dread, and mystery the entire time. I had to keep reading to find out what happened! There is an element of not knowing what is real and what’s not that the reader shares with the characters. This is an excellent spooky read. <br/><br/>There</span>
  <span id="freeText2742709339015582755" style="display:none">TW: all your typical horror stuff - death, gore, ghosts, etc <br /><br />This was a WILD ride. I don’t remember the last time I binge read a book so fast. I very rarely read anything close to horror (and this is as close as I get!) but this maintained a sense of eerie foreboding, dread, and mystery the entire time. I had to keep reading to find out what happened! There is an element of not knowing what is real and what’s not that the reader shares with the characters. This is an excellent spooky read. <br /><br />There were some things I don’t think were quite as strong. Some things were left unexplained that I would have liked to know more about (but also maybe there’s a point to that). There were also some things about the fantasy elements that were a little outlandish for me. And the romance was just not something I cared about in the midst of all the suspense. But overall, a solid spooky story. </span>

<div id="review_2980780728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2980780728" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2980780728?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=2019-publications">2019-publications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2980780728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18062341388191193525">This is an exciting YA fantasy driven by a compelling atmosphere and a dark mystery case. I was pulled in pretty quickly and was curious to see how this author would retell one of my all time favourite fairy tales. When I was a kid, all I wanted to watch was Barbie’s adaptation of the Twelve Dancing Princesses. I have fond memories of sitting in my room and gazing in adoration at the different dresses and shoes. Fashion is not an important component of this story and you won’t find any Barbies i</span>
  <span id="freeText18062341388191193525" style="display:none">This is an exciting YA fantasy driven by a compelling atmosphere and a dark mystery case. I was pulled in pretty quickly and was curious to see how this author would retell one of my all time favourite fairy tales. When I was a kid, all I wanted to watch was Barbie’s adaptation of the Twelve Dancing Princesses. I have fond memories of sitting in my room and gazing in adoration at the different dresses and shoes. Fashion is not an important component of this story and you won’t find any Barbies in it either. It’s a dark story with death creeping around every corner. The heroine—Annaleigh—is doing her best to shed light on the darkness but there are powerful forces at play so it will take courage, strength and determination to unveil the mystery.<br /><br />I really enjoyed my experience reading this fantasy. Annaleigh is the kind of heroine dimensional enough to be real but also one that takes the place of the reader in a way. So as I was reading this book I really felt like I was Annaleigh most of the time. Her reactions are very universal and she is a teenager through and through. She is exactly like the kinds of heroines I was interested in in my early teens because I could picture myself in their places easily, embarking on all of these crazy adventures. Now, the secondary characters blur into one another, which is unfortunate because this could have been such a strong story about sisterhood. But since the sisters themselves are not memorable—in their actions or personalities—I wasn’t affected by them much. <br /><br />This book is a crazy, almost mystical, ride that I’m sure you’ll be swept in. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18062341388191193525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2713206707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2713206707" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2713206707?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=arcs-reviewed">arcs-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2713206707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6661239986288681464">Extremely atmospheric, haunting, and filled with historically tinged Gothic horror, this was something else.<br/><br/><b>World:</b> ★★★★ 1/2<br/><b>Plot Execution:</b> ★★★ 1/2<br/><b>Character Development:</b> ★★★<br/><b>Gothic Ocean Vibes:</b> ★★★★★<br/><br/>Well hello, Gothic ocean-inspired fairy tale retelling! <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> was something I never knew I wanted until I read it. It's a full cast list of sisters and other residents of Highmoor Estate, located on one of several islands that are home to the People of the Salt. One by one, the sist</span>
  <span id="freeText6661239986288681464" style="display:none">Extremely atmospheric, haunting, and filled with historically tinged Gothic horror, this was something else.<br /><br /><b>World:</b> ★★★★ 1/2<br /><b>Plot Execution:</b> ★★★ 1/2<br /><b>Character Development:</b> ★★★<br /><b>Gothic Ocean Vibes:</b> ★★★★★<br /><br />Well hello, Gothic ocean-inspired fairy tale retelling! <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> was something I never knew I wanted until I read it. It's a full cast list of sisters and other residents of Highmoor Estate, located on one of several islands that are home to the People of the Salt. One by one, the sisters are succumbing to mysterious deaths. Something spooky and magical is AFOOT. <br /><br />Annaleigh Thaumas is the second oldest of the surviving sisters. Annaleigh doesn't believe all of her sisters are dying accidentally. With a distinctively historical flair, <b>Annaleigh embarks on a whodunit narrative to find out who killed the last one her sisters, Eulalie, and find out if the rumors about her family are true—is the Thaumas family cursed?</b> <br /><br /><b>I loved Annaleigh.</b> She was full of character, inquisitive but not aggressive, and felt grounded in her historical time period. <b>Unlike other YA heroines who feel like modern characters plunked into historical settings, Annaleigh was very much grounded in her time.</b> <br /><br />In the midst of Annaleigh's quest to find her sisters' murderer, another plot is bubbling. <b>The group of remaining sisters and Annaleigh find a "portal" of sorts on the grounds of their estate that leads them to anywhere they mentally desire.</b> The sisters find ball after ball through the portal, dancing their nights away with strangers in glittering settings....but is there something sinister under the surface?<br /><br /><b>As the nights continue and the girls burn through their dancing shoes, Annaleigh begins to suspect that there is something wrong with the portal, Highmoor, and the people around her.</b> <br /><br /><b>In a traditional YA move,</b> we are also introduced to a love triangle. <b>While I initially was bored and underwhelmed by its introduction to the plot, this love triangle quickly gained several layers</b> and actually became incredibly spooky and (surprisingly?) terrifying. <br /><br />I loved this dark story. <b><i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> is equal parts murder mystery, ghost story, sweet dream/beautiful nightmare, and an extremely dark rendition of the Twelve Dancing Princesses fairy tale.</b> It's a lot for one concept, but it works.<br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to Random House Children's via NetGalley for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6661239986288681464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2926623386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2926623386" />
    <a title="Arini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39722464-arini"><img alt="Arini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565922259p2/39722464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2926623386?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arini" href="/user/show/39722464-arini">Arini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781984831941" href="/book/show/42766937-house-of-salt-and-sorrows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2926623386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17820544561792226647"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584410869i/29116483._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>3.75 Stars</b><br/><br/>This book threw me a curve, and I was left in a fumble. Unsure of which direction I should go to catch the ball. Damn, unreliable narrator! Also, idk if it’s my <b>creepy meter</b> that’s low compare to the rest of you mystery/thriller booknuts out there, but this book creeped me the hell out alright. The fact that this is a retelling doesn’t make it any less unique and magical. On the surface, it looks wildly similar to the original tale of <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses,</i> but on a deeper leve</span>
  <span id="freeText17820544561792226647" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584410869i/29116483._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3.75 Stars</b><br><br>This book threw me a curve, and I was left in a fumble. Unsure of which direction I should go to catch the ball. Damn, unreliable narrator! Also, idk if it’s my <b>creepy meter</b> that’s low compare to the rest of you mystery/thriller booknuts out there, but this book creeped me the hell out alright. The fact that this is a retelling doesn’t make it any less unique and magical. On the surface, it looks wildly similar to the original tale of <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses,</i> but on a deeper level this book has its own appeal that makes it all the more remarkable in its own right.<br><br><blockquote>↬ <b>Intriguing plot</b><br><br>The mystery element of the story is my favorite part of the book. Annaleigh’s ghostly visions really help set the somber tone. You can feel the spookiness. It makes your brows crease in worry and your spines tingle with uneasiness.<br><br>↬ <b>Mesmerizing world building</b><br><br>I loved the setting and the world building in this book. The big mansion added with the ancient and horror feel to it, made me feel like I was watching <i>The Haunting of Hill House</i> all over again. In addition, the sea and the port market gave me the <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> vibes. I loved the concept behind all the different islands and the gods and the religions. The magic made me feel like being inside a fairy tale.<br><br>↬ <b>Unpredictable but bland characters</b><br><br><b><i>Annaleigh</i></b> is such an unreliable narrator. You’d feel like you’re being toyed with bcs she pulls you into all different directions. I loved that about her, but at the same time it was also a little frustrating. It doesn’t matter if you have your own theory about who the culprit is bcs she’ll make you doubt it.<br><br>As for the rest of the characters, I was a bit concerned about how I was going to remember them all at first. Thankfully, each of them quickly grew on me as I read on although I do think that the triplets and the Graces could just easily be merged as one character. My favorite sister is definitely <b><i>Verity</i></b> (one of the youngests), and my least favorite one is <b><i>Camille</i></b> (the oldest).<br><br>↬ <b>Underdeveloped romance</b><br><br>The romance in this book is not my favorite, but I also don’t hate it. I thought it was sketchy at the beginning. Cassius for me is just a <i>meh</i> love interest. I feel like he has no purpose other than to confuse the readers with more suspect theories. The romance between him and Annaleigh is unconvincing as it lacks any sort ot tension, emotional connection, and build up.<br><br>↬ <b>Lyrical writing and steady pacing</b><br><br>For the majority of the book, the writing is lyrical and flowy and real. It just makes you feel like you’re engrossed in a movie. However, there are other times when I felt a little baffled by the absurdity of a couple scenes. The first 1/3 of the book is a bit slow with only a few drops of hints here and there. After that, it shifts to a steadier pace.</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Overall thoughts</u>
</b>:<br><br>This book is the kind of dark fantasy retelling that I didn’t know I needed. We’re all so used to disney princesses retelings, but now we have this one that’s just as impressive and special (if not more) as the rest. It’s got all the ingredients to make an atmospheric and tantalizing story. We have the mystery, the haunted house, the ghosts, the vivid and terrorizing visions, the family curse and dynamic, the star-crossed lovers type of romance, the magical door and dancing shoes, the bizarre deaths, and yeah, you get me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17820544561792226647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2948873540" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15585288535359861121"><b>2.5/5</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/thevillainsquest/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | full review on <a href='https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCREgLpjZ0Z3atGT6JBO1i-g?view_as=subscriber' rel='nofollow noopener'>youtube</a><br/><br/><i>Yikes.</i> Let's all grab a drink because shit is about to get SERIOUS.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567284003ra/28080924.gif' width='250' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Another book that could have gone under a couple more editing rounds. <br/><br/>1.	Character development: Do I remember the name of the main character? No. It's so minimalist that I couldn’t see it. It’s like expensive invisible and uncomfortable furniture for rich people. An excuse to make money and the void in art. <br/><br/>2.	Worldbuilding: thin like a prostitute’s panties. Just like character development.</span>
  <span id="freeText15585288535359861121" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thevillainsquest/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | full review on <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCREgLpjZ0Z3atGT6JBO1i-g?view_as=subscriber" rel="nofollow noopener">youtube</a><br><br><i>Yikes.</i> Let's all grab a drink because shit is about to get SERIOUS.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567284003ra/28080924.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another book that could have gone under a couple more editing rounds. <br><br>1.	Character development: Do I remember the name of the main character? No. It's so minimalist that I couldn’t see it. It’s like expensive invisible and uncomfortable furniture for rich people. An excuse to make money and the void in art. <br><br>2.	Worldbuilding: thin like a prostitute’s panties. Just like character development. <br><br>3.	Writing style. It’s there I guess I would have sworn that writing used to be the priority of books. Guess I was wrong. <br><br>4.	Romance: *laughs* well that sure was there. 100% It was unnecessary, cringe, and stupid and incomprehensible. Think about the least appealing thing in the world, wherever it’s your dad naked, I don’t care, but yeah, that’s exactly the romance in the book. <br><br>5.	The villain: probably one of the worst villain I’ve ever read and seen in my life. And I’ve watched the Mandarin in Iron Man, so you’d think the bar for worst villains was high. You’d think that, in a murder mystery, the villain would AT LEAST take as much space as the UNECESSARY ROMANCE TO THE RESOLUTION OF THE STORY. But NOOOOOOOOO. Let us be so shook by the existence and motivations of the “villain” because that sure would work as a plot twist. <br><br>Anyway, that’s it for this review. Hopes it convinced you not to pick up this book. If you still want to read it then, honestly it’s like doing heroine after everyone told you it was the worst drug. After coke. <br><br>If you want to hear more of my thoughts on this book, here's the <a href="https://youtu.be/NsxB6e7GAqc" rel="nofollow noopener">full rant</a><br><br></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=blank-of-blank-and-blank">blank-of-blank-and-blank</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=les-arcs-de-triomphes">les-arcs-de-triomphes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2958735929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14025990958444248459"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/>I have developed my following by being 100% honest, whether or not a book is popular. I think this is especially important in the YA genre, when many books are over-hyped in a way that comes across as incredibly artificial and manufactured at times. I'm sorry, but you can't all be the #1 best-selling YA book, especially not if you're all doubling down on the BLANK of BLANK AND BLANK forgettable title game. I mean, <i>come on</i>. I can barely </span>
  <span id="freeText14025990958444248459" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br>I have developed my following by being 100% honest, whether or not a book is popular. I think this is especially important in the YA genre, when many books are over-hyped in a way that comes across as incredibly artificial and manufactured at times. I'm sorry, but you can't all be the #1 best-selling YA book, especially not if you're all doubling down on the BLANK of BLANK AND BLANK forgettable title game. I mean, <i>come on</i>. I can barely remember my own name half the time, let alone a baker's dozen worth of best-selling YA titles that all sound virtually the same.<br><br><br><br>HOUSE OF SALT AND SORROWS appealed to me, in spite of my misgivings, because of several things. 1) it's a faerie-tale retelling and I love those. I love them a lot, in fact. I was raised on faerie-tales from all over the world, and I will never stop feeling that same magic and mysticism from reading them. 2) it is a gothic novel and if you have been following me at all, you <i>know </i>how much I love me a dark and creepy novel set in some crumbling manor home on a cliff and peopled with ghosts. It's bomb. Combined? That's a c-c-c-combo breaker to the MAX.<br><br><br><br>The book is about a girl named Annaleigh. She and her sisters are the daughters of this incredibly rich dude who lives in a crumbling manor home on a cliff. Her sisters are dropping like flies, beginning with the death of their mother, and some say it's because of a curse. We meet them when they're all gathered at the funeral of their latest dead sister, and mood is grim. Helpful and oblivious stepmother Morella thinks it's time that morning be over because she's preggers and wants to party. Never mind that she is the same age as her stepdaughters and they'd so Parent Trap her sorry behind if their mother was still alive. As it is, they're stuck with her, but at least they get new shoes out of it.<br><br><br><br>Mysteriously, the new shoes end up tattered within a week. And other weird things start happening. Images of their dead sisters. Parties that nobody remembers. Suspicious deaths. A love triangle-- oops, scrap that last one. That's not weird at all, just par for the course in YA land. A whole bunch of other stuff happened, too, but I skimmed the middle of this book pretty heavily because I wasn't really amused by the sad descriptions of the heroines lackluster attempts at Nancy Drewing.<br><br><br><br>In the last act, the book manages to valiantly rise to the task of bringing this book to conclusion. There are some truly creepy scenes in here, and honestly if the whole book had been like that, this could have been a four- or even five-star read for me. If you've read this, you know what I mean. That ballroom scene. YES. I also think the author could have played up the use of the creepy masked man, instead of having him pop up only twice and immediately be a figure of suspicion. That's the problem; if the middle is SUPER boring, I'm going to jump on exciting things when they happen, and everything is going to seem super obvious. I figured out the "surprise" twist right away.<br><br><br><br>The writing in here is decent and the author is capable of setting the mood well when she so chooses. But someone-- the editor-- should have cut about 100 pages from this book and had the author rewrite the beginning to be more suspenseful. Likewise, there was some inconsistent characterization in this book, as Heather pointed out in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2965807617" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a>. Morella was all over the place, as were several of the sisters, and the father went from being an oblivious patsy to kind of abusive and scary? As I said, foreshadowing would have fixed ALL of this and made the ending feel less... convenient.<br><br><br><br>I was going to give this book a 2-star review, but the ending sufficiently wowed me enough that I feel like I can be generous and award a paltry half-star. I'm definitely not blown away by this like some of the other preliminary reviews were, though, and while this author is definitely a cut above the rest when it comes to some of the other BLANK of BLANK and BLANK authors, I'm not sure I loved this enough that I'd instantly race out to acquire anything else she writes. But maybe. The jury is still out on this one. My rating, however, is decided.<br><br><br><br><i>Thanks to the publisher for sending me a copy in exchange for an honest review!</i><br><br><br><br>2.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_2933126124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
