        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2933126124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10485839276082284688">House of Salt and Sorrows is a hot topic ever since it came out, and it was hyped for months before it’s release.<br/>I was lucky enough to have an opportunity to read it via Netgalley and I can tell you, I completely understand where the hype comes from.<br/><br/>This story really impressed me and even though it is a retelling of a tale of Twelve Dancing Princesses I would say it is one of the most unique books that I have read in the past few months. However, I have to stress out that I am not familiar with </span>
  <span id="freeText10485839276082284688" style="display:none">House of Salt and Sorrows is a hot topic ever since it came out, and it was hyped for months before it’s release.<br />I was lucky enough to have an opportunity to read it via Netgalley and I can tell you, I completely understand where the hype comes from.<br /><br />This story really impressed me and even though it is a retelling of a tale of Twelve Dancing Princesses I would say it is one of the most unique books that I have read in the past few months. However, I have to stress out that I am not familiar with the original fairy tale nor did I watch the Barbie movie.<br /><br />The atmosphere was spooky and I loved it so much. I like how the story became darker and darker as it progressed, that closer to the end it even had some horror elements.<br />The atmosphere was my favorite part of the novel.<br /><br />What I found funny was how at some points Highmoor people gave me that Greyjoy vibes (Game of Thrones reference), and it almost felt like they were cousins (their funeral rituals are so similar that I couldn’t help myself but laugh, but in a good way).<br /><br />The main character Annaleigh was likeable and it was easy to connect with her. I enjoyed following the story from her perspective and I also really liked her relationship with her older sister Camilla.<br />I was also fascinated with their stepmother and wanted to know more about her.<br />As for other characters, I have to admit that I wish they had more substance to them, because they felt pretty much dull and I had hard time to recognize one sister from the other.<br /><br />One of the big reveals (how they went to the dances) blew my mind and in my opinion, it was the best part of the story.<br /><br />I was also very happy with the way this story ended, including all the dark and spooky elements.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading House of Salt and Sorrows and I would like to read other work by Erin A. Craig.<br /><br />I highly recommend this one to lovers of young adult fantasy and spooky stories.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Read this and more reviews on my blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookdustmagic.com">https://bookdustmagic.com</a> </b>
</i></span>

<div id="review_2933697379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2933697379" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2933697379?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=owl-crate-books">owl-crate-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2933697379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9060296771390137673"><b>YA Fantasy at its best - dark, mysterious and hauntingly beautiful!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>This retelling of The Twelve Dancing Princesses is an absolute winner!</i>
</b> Erin A. Craig brought this gothic and mystical world to life - I mean it literally leaps off the page! I had such a clear vision of Highmoor, the sea, the balls and the sisters in my mind. It was all so atmospheric and enchanting. <br/><br/>I also thoroughly enjoyed the writing. It was dark for YA - full of foreboding, mystery, and a rather creepy (almost gruesome) </span>
  <span id="freeText9060296771390137673" style="display:none"><b>YA Fantasy at its best - dark, mysterious and hauntingly beautiful!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>This retelling of The Twelve Dancing Princesses is an absolute winner!</i>
</b> Erin A. Craig brought this gothic and mystical world to life - I mean it literally leaps off the page! I had such a clear vision of Highmoor, the sea, the balls and the sisters in my mind. It was all so atmospheric and enchanting. <br /><br />I also thoroughly enjoyed the writing. It was dark for YA - full of foreboding, mystery, and a rather creepy (almost gruesome) ghostly vibe which I loved. Annaleigh was a character that the intended audience can easily identify with - strong, family oriented and full of heart. <br /><br />Did I have it figured out? Ultimately, Yes. Did that detract from my enjoyment? Absolutely Not! There were some great twists and turns here that I didn't see coming. I know I am not the intended age/audience for these books and yet, I unabashedly love them. This book was easy to get lost in. I read it mostly in 1 sitting and it proved to be an enchanting page-turner. I couldn't wait to get to the end to see if my plot predictions were correct. <br /><br /><b>All in all, this was a strong debut novel. Erin Craig creates a dark, enchanting world that you can easily get lost in. I can't wait to see what else we get from this author in the future!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9060296771390137673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2623948997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2623948997" />
    <a title="Acqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47160872-acqua"><img alt="Acqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548417878p2/47160872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2623948997?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Acqua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Acqua" href="/user/show/47160872-acqua">Acqua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=love-cover">love-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=love-polygons">love-polygons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=mystery-th-su">mystery-th-su</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=needed-subtlety">needed-subtlety</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2623948997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13754083883240768639"><b>This book doesn't get that heterosexuality is not a personality trait.</b><br/><br/>I'm not saying this to be funny: <b>no one in this book had a personality</b>. I can't tell you anything about the main character apart from the fact that she's attracted to Cassius and cares for her sisters; she was more a placeholder than a character. The boys were even worse, existing in the book just to be handsome, vaguely mysterious, and exchange <b>possessive glares that the book will carefully specify are masculine</b> while fightin</span>
  <span id="freeText13754083883240768639" style="display:none"><b>This book doesn't get that heterosexuality is not a personality trait.</b><br /><br />I'm not saying this to be funny: <b>no one in this book had a personality</b>. I can't tell you anything about the main character apart from the fact that she's attracted to Cassius and cares for her sisters; she was more a placeholder than a character. The boys were even worse, existing in the book just to be handsome, vaguely mysterious, and exchange <b>possessive glares that the book will carefully specify are masculine</b> while fighting for the main girl.<br />And while I knew, getting into a <i>Twelve Dancing Princesses</i> retelling, that not every sister was going to be developed, I didn't expect their attraction to boys to replace the personality of all of them (in the older ones; the younger one is never anything more than a "creepy little girl" stereotype.)<br />Four sisters are dead at the beginning of the book, and the living ones are worried not because of that, or not because maybe they're going to die next - but because their supposed "curse" scares men away and <b>they think they're going to grow old and die <i>unkissed</i>, without ever having danced with a boy</b>.<br />Yeah. Priorities!<br /><br /><b>So, let's be kind and say that this book is plot-driven.</b><br />The plot wasn't that great. <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> is a gothic mystery with a really interesting premise and solid background, but the execution ended up being really messy. <b>All the tension relied on the usual "is the main character *gasp* <i>insane</i> or is that magic?" trope, which is cheap</b> and I hate it, especially when the answer is so obvious and when the book constantly approached even only the possibility of mental illness in really insensitive ways.<br />By the way, in case that wasn't already clear: there is no diversity whatsoever in this book. The whole cast is all-straight, and, unless I missed something, also all-white and all-abled (which: the realism, where?). There's one old blind man whose entire personality was "crazy" who appeared for half a scene, and that's it. <b>No diversity, bland unnecessary romance, love triangle... did we all somehow time-travel to 2013?</b><br /><br /><b>The mystery was kind of underwhelming, but it wasn't terrible</b>. The foreshadowing was somewhat unsubtle and heavy-handed at times, but it didn't give away the whole story immediately as many YA mystery books do; the revelation wasn't the most unpredictable thing ever, but it was fine - I was mostly annoyed by how rushed the resolution was, and especially <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[by how rushed the apparition of not one plot-relevant god but <i>multiple plot-relevant gods</i> was <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><b>And I still didn't dislike this, not really.</b><br />I mean, I clearly had many problems with it, but the thing is, it kept my interest. I'm barely reading these days and I finished it really quickly - which yes, that also means that there wasn't much substance to it, but <b>it was a fun ride most of the time, and I wanted to know what happened</b>. I never really thought about DNFing it.<br /><br />Another reason I didn't dislike this book is that <b>I got into it for the island gothic aesthetic, and in that aspect, it didn't disappoint at all.</b><br />Have you ever watched a movie or a show in which the acting was bad and the plot was mediocre but the setting and the costume design made it worth watching at least once, purely as eye candy? <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i> is the book version of that. The descriptions are beautiful, and the island atmosphere is perfect. <b>I loved all the mentions of coastal marine life, the descriptions of tide pools, all the details this book gave me about buildings and dresses and shoes and accessories</b>.<br /><br />This is deeply forgettable and really flawed, and not something I would ever reread, but it was worth reading once just for that. <b>2.5 stars.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13754083883240768639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2807288084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2807288084" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14081543-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554746625p2/14081543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2807288084?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/14081543-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2807288084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5963568429821117391"><i>ARC received by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><b>This book was a total mind f**k.</b> <br/> <br/>Fantasy/horror/thriller/murder mystery...it was glorious. I'm usually not into murder mysteries or thrillers, but the fantasy aspect made it AMAZING. <br/> <br/>The story follows Annaleigh, one of (originally) twelve sisters. The family is in perpetual mourning as sister after sister dies, leading the town to believe the family is cursed. The summary of the book talks about pretty dresses and dan</span>
  <span id="freeText5963568429821117391" style="display:none"><i>ARC received by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br /><b>This book was a total mind f**k.</b> <br /> <br />Fantasy/horror/thriller/murder mystery...it was glorious. I'm usually not into murder mysteries or thrillers, but the fantasy aspect made it AMAZING. <br /> <br />The story follows Annaleigh, one of (originally) twelve sisters. The family is in perpetual mourning as sister after sister dies, leading the town to believe the family is cursed. The summary of the book talks about pretty dresses and dancing at balls, but it is not as frilly as just that. The reason behind all of the frillyness is actually quite dark and twisted.<br /> <br /><b>I enjoyed every minute of reading <i>House of Salt and Sorrows</i>, and I found it particularly enjoyable on dark and stormy nights.</b> It was incredibly suspenseful and I was pleasantly surprised that my eyes were glued to the page. Not because I just enjoy binge reading things, but because I had to know what happened next. And not just at the end. But from moment to moment. This book is filled with so many twists and turns and had such an EXCELLENT way of portraying distortions in reality that I found myself pausing and being like, <b>"WTF? Is this happening? Did that really happen? It seems like it happened? WHAT IS HAPPENING?!"</b><br /> <br />Over and over and over again I thought I knew who the killer must be. As I got further into the book, I genuinely had NO clue who could be behind everything. This is in part due to Craig's amazing characterization, giving us well-rounded, flawed characters with so much depth that you feel like you know them. <br /><br />This book is thrilling and captivating!<b> If you are looking for something spooky but still need your fantasy fix, then you will love this!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5963568429821117391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br/><br/><br/>This book, although a bit clichéd, basically contains every single thing I absolutely love about books and I'm not sure how many scares I got or how many times my heart broke while I was reading it, but it's now one of my favorite reads of all t</span>
  <span id="freeText13077386371462553299" style="display:none"><i>“Flushed with starlight and moonlight drowned,<br>All the dreamers are castle-bound.<br>At midnight’s stroke, we will unwind,<br>Revealing fantasies soft or unkind.<br>Show me debauched nightmares or sunniest daydreams.<br>Come not as you are but as you wish to be seen.”</i><br><br><br><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg" alt="banner-di-bobi.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>This book, although a bit clichéd, basically contains every single thing I absolutely love about books and I'm not sure how many scares I got or how many times my heart broke while I was reading it, but it's now one of my favorite reads of all times and I'll probably never recover from its dark, twisted beauty.<br><br>I also just found out Erin A. Craig started writing this book shortly after her daughter was born and I've got to give her all the kudos for this because she managed to give birth to a masterpiece after a masterpiece, and here I am, 13 months later and I still don't have the time/energy to write coherent reviews.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13077386371462553299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2901388284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2901388284" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2901388284?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2901388284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539111677849041220">Craig's debut frames the Grimms' tale of twelve dancing princesses as a Gothic murder mystery. Laced gowns and mourning garb, fairy shoes and midnight balls, reanimated corpses and whispers in the dark, crashing seas and the taste of salt in the air. There's a lot to love here, but the plot suffers from slow pacing and a lack of suspense that doesn't build until the final chapters. <br/><blockquote>
  <i>Nestled on a bed of navy velvet were my shoes. I'd selected a jade leather, and the cobbler had added glittering</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8539111677849041220" style="display:none">Craig's debut frames the Grimms' tale of twelve dancing princesses as a Gothic murder mystery. Laced gowns and mourning garb, fairy shoes and midnight balls, reanimated corpses and whispers in the dark, crashing seas and the taste of salt in the air. There's a lot to love here, but the plot suffers from slow pacing and a lack of suspense that doesn't build until the final chapters. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Nestled on a bed of navy velvet were my shoes. I'd selected a jade leather, and the cobbler had added glittering seafoam and silver bits, concentrated heavily at the toes, then fading as they swept across the slipper. They would match my gown perfectly.*</i>
</blockquote><br />-<br />*Note: Quote taken from an Advanced Reader's Copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8539111677849041220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/uvGgFhGZu0vToVZPAgwibjcWuGa3d0tuJ8aEFvQVaBThfmAt25kaikyfdjqHEZg/HeDx+aIh+YXX+4IXpPrFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iXi8icpWlbkN75Apqtm7khQKFxd7vxAvBgC9z1wGlKAkFoOJJX6XPguTaKh8zc17UKHOMQfqSuSpwEnXWUUqFw==')})
  }
//]]>

But when she receives her first royal patron—Rook, the autumn prince—Isobel makes a deadly mistake. She paints mortal sorrow in his eyes, a weakness that could cost him his throne, and even his life.\n\nFurious, Rook spirits Isobel away to his kingdom to stand trial for her crime. But something is seriously amiss in his world, and they are attacked from every side. With Isobel and Rook depending upon each other for survival, their alliance blossoms into trust, perhaps even love . . . a forbidden emotion that would violate the fair folks’ ruthless laws, rendering both their lives forfeit. What force could Isobel\'s paintings conjure that is powerful enough to defy the ancient malice of the fairy courts?\n\nIsobel and Rook journey along a knife-edge in a lush world where beauty masks <span id="freeTextContainer5737040256524795986">New York Times bestselling author Erin A. Craig has always loved telling stories.<br/><br/>After getting her B.F.A. from the University of Michigan, in Theatre Design and Production, she stage managed tragic operas with hunchbacks, séances, and murderous clowns, then decided she wanted to write books that were just as spooky.<br/><br/>An avid reader, decent embroiderer, rabid basketball fan, and collector of typewrit</span>
  <span id="freeText5737040256524795986" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Erin A. Craig has always loved telling stories.<br /><br />After getting her B.F.A. from the University of Michigan, in Theatre Design and Production, she stage managed tragic operas with hunchbacks, séances, and murderous clowns, then decided she wanted to write books that were just as spooky.<br /><br />An avid reader, decent embroiderer, rabid basketball fan, and collector of typewriters, Erin makes her home in West Michigan with her husband and daughter.<br /><br />She is represented by Sarah Landis at Sterling Lord Literistic.</span>
